<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_cd061454-e017-4f28-a677-83970de1c8d1'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText2869140399380220912" style="display:none">Dark schemes unfold--and Sophie's loyalty is pushed to the limit--in this thrilling fifth book in the best-selling KEEPER OF THE LOST CITIES SERIES. <br /><br />Sophie Foster is back in the Lost Cities--but the Lost Cities have changed. The threat of war hangs heavy over her glittering world, and the Neverseen are wreaking havoc. <br /> <br />The lines between friend and enemy have blurred, and Sophie is unsure whom to trust. But when she's warned that the people she loves most will be the next victims, she knows she has to act. <br /><br />A mysterious symbol could be the key--if only she knew how to translate it. Every new clue seems to lead deeper into her world's underbelly and the Black Swan aren't the only ones who have plans. The Neverseen have their own Initiative, and if Sophie doesn't stop it, they might finally have the ultimate means to control her.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12904855647455981843">Reread: 1/6/18<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>Hey, all the cool kids are sleeping with stuffed animals these days.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Once again, Shannon Messenger has left me staring at the cover of her book, astonished. One surprise after another. That's what <i>Lodestar</i> was about. Not one character in this book hasn't changed in some way. I'm beginning to enjoy Linh's quiet personality, but Tam reminds me a bit too much of Keefe. And...I'm not a huge fan of Keefe. Especially now. As for Fitz, I never cared too much about him- until now, where</span>
  <span id="freeText12904855647455981843" style="display:none">Reread: 1/6/18<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Hey, all the cool kids are sleeping with stuffed animals these days.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Once again, Shannon Messenger has left me staring at the cover of her book, astonished. One surprise after another. That's what <i>Lodestar</i> was about. Not one character in this book hasn't changed in some way. I'm beginning to enjoy Linh's quiet personality, but Tam reminds me a bit too much of Keefe. And...I'm not a huge fan of Keefe. Especially now. As for Fitz, I never cared too much about him- until now, where I'm proud to consider him one of my favorite middle-grade heroes.<br /><br />But of course Messenger <i>had</i> to end <i>Lodestar</i> on a cliffhanger. I wonder if she's met Rick Riordan before...<br /><br />Also, did Shannon Messenger read my "before reading" review or something...?<br /><br /><i>"You can ignore it all you want, Foster, but sooner or later you're going to have to solve the love triangle. Or should we get real and call it a square?"</i><br /><br />The romance is escalating, yet Sophie remains oblivious. Don't you just love when that happens?<br /><br />BEFORE READING:<br />If Shannon Messenger creates a more distinct love triangle between Sophie, Fitz, and Keefe I'm going to die. D:<br /><br />Or what if she creates a love <i>square</i>?</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1426450635" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1426450635" />
    <a title="Mossring" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36697449-mossring"><img alt="Mossring" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490456347p2/36697449.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1426450635?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mossring" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mossring" href="/user/show/36697449-mossring">Mossring</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1426450635" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16573901638402016758"><blockquote>
  <i>Actions never tell the whole story. Good can be done for the wrong reason. And bad can be misunderstood.</i>
</blockquote><br/>I've been a fan of the Keeper of the Lost Cities series for nearly two years now. I know all the books by heart. I know what I expect from each passing book. <b>And yet, the fifth book might be my least favourite of the series.</b> <br/><br/>Let's start off with the things I found pleasant in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27272698.Lodestar__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities__5_' title='Lodestar (Keeper of the Lost Cities #5) by Shannon Messenger' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lodestar</a>. One good thing I really admire in the series is the<b> incredible world building and the slowly escalating p</b></span>
  <span id="freeText16573901638402016758" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Actions never tell the whole story. Good can be done for the wrong reason. And bad can be misunderstood.</i>
</blockquote><br />I've been a fan of the Keeper of the Lost Cities series for nearly two years now. I know all the books by heart. I know what I expect from each passing book. <b>And yet, the fifth book might be my least favourite of the series.</b> <br /><br />Let's start off with the things I found pleasant in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27272698.Lodestar__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities__5_" title="Lodestar (Keeper of the Lost Cities #5) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Lodestar</a>. One good thing I really admire in the series is the<b> incredible world building and the slowly escalating plot</b>, which seems to get thicker and more complex by each book, keeping readers enraptured and entertained. We get to learn more of the Lost Cities and its history and culture, and how it connects with the present. This book manages to top off all its predecessors in terms of the conflict in the plot-line and the extent at which both the Council and the Neverseen are willing to go.<br /><br />But that's one thing that I'm troubled about. In this book, the Council has stepped up their game, and so has the Neverseen. However, the Black Swan, the perspective the story is told in, didn't really seem to do anything at all, except for Prentice-related activities. The rest of the plot is pushed on by the new horrible, gory things the Neverseen has done, and the Black Swan merely comes in to solve the mysteries surrounding the Neverseen <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[which concerns their mysterious symbol and Cyrah's death <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Since the story is told in Sophie's point of view, which is the perspective of the Black Swan, <b>the story seemed rather dull in comparison with the last book</b>, when Sophie and her friends had destroyed Ravagog on their own. The climax in this story only happened with the Council's permission, lessening the potential suspense that could've happened.<br /><br />And maybe that's what I find unappealing about the plot of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27272698.Lodestar__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities__5_" title="Lodestar (Keeper of the Lost Cities #5) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Lodestar</a>. <b>I felt like it lacked a sort of emotion, as it had been overshadowed by the plot</b>. For example, the first book of the series was in the perspective of a scared, but excited girl who was completely new to a different world. The second book was narrated by a fearful, grieving girl who felt useless, but she was still determined to save a person whom she loved. The third book and the fourth book were filled with much stronger emotion which was triggered by the slowly thickening plot. <br /><br />Which leads us to the fifth book, which I felt was<b> lacking in character development and the progression and growth of the relationships between the characters</b>. There was some insight into Dex and his family, which I appreciated, but other than that, it just fell flat. <br /><br />Biana and Linh had no major role to play in the plot, especially Linh, which makes me very disappointed, because they are the only other two female characters that have the opportunity to play a huge part in the plot besides Sophie. <b>Tam and Linh felt especially lacking in character development</b>, which is really sad for me because they're my favourite characters and I would've wanted to see a stronger representation of what they could be. So far, their characters remain undeveloped, and I hope Shannon Messenger can make them realer, and actually include them in the plot. <br /><br />Only Sophie, Fitz, and Keefe were actually in the plot, which is sad because not everything revolves around the characters involved in the love triangle, however entertaining and amusing it is.<br /><br /><b>The only relationship I could really relate to and feel for was that between Sophie and Keefe. </b>Their interaction lessens in this book, but I feel that they are really the couple readers should be rooting for. Sophie's determination and desperation to believe in and trust Keefe showed itself clearly throughout the novel. Keefe also experiences determination and desperation, but it is for different reasons, as he wants to infiltrate the Neverseen while doing his best to protect his friends, most especially Sophie, from danger and harm. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"It is kinda nice having someone look out for me."<br /><br />"You don't make it easy."<br /><br />"Another thing you and I have in common."<br /><br />His floating thoughts made it clear how determined he was to protect her. It made her heart somehow both light and heavy at the same time.</i>
</blockquote><br />Even though Fitz 'steps up his game' in this book, I found their relationship bland and forced, and <b>I personally had an overdose of Fitz</b> in this book. <br /><br />...Well, I am on Team Foster-Keefe after all, but that's not the point.<br /><br />There are <i>quite</i> a lot of character deaths in this book, and one person was heavily injured. <br /><br />Spoiler alert: Prentice is <i>still</i> not healed. I can't be the only one who's exasperated and impatient, after thinking he'd be healed in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27272698.Lodestar__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities__5_" title="Lodestar (Keeper of the Lost Cities #5) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Lodestar</a>.<br /><br /> The final death is probably the reason I gave this book an extra star, just so because I love suffering and crying. Yep, I practically bawled when the death happened. First time a book made me cry, so it definitely deserves an extra star and a kudos, especially with that cliffhanger ending. That was obviously written to make us suffer in suspense. It was also a consolation gift for the horrible character development.<br /><br />Shannon, please don't disappoint me again with the sixth book. Also, petition for Dex and Linh to be on the cover. My two cinnamon rolls deserve to be on the cover and you can't say otherwise.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16573901638402016758" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2956920503" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2956920503" />
    <a title="BrooKe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87485390-brooke"><img alt="BrooKe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583732525p2/87485390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2956920503?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BrooKe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BrooKe" href="/user/show/87485390-brooke">BrooKe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2956920503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6097977634878930458">3.9/5 | In which everyone knows wassup between Sophie and Keefe except Sophie (and Fitz, poor boy). <br/><br/>It’s hard to believe that this is only the fifth instalment out of, what, ten planned books? That’s only halfway through (behold my mathematic <i>genius</i>) and already so much has happened! And that’s only all we know of; <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5265998.Shannon_Messenger' title='Shannon Messenger' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shannon Messenger</a> stated she’d put out Keeper books for as long as she could. Part of me is worried that the quality might deteriorate if the series goes on too long but another part </span>
  <span id="freeText6097977634878930458" style="display:none">3.9/5 | In which everyone knows wassup between Sophie and Keefe except Sophie (and Fitz, poor boy). <br /><br />It’s hard to believe that this is only the fifth instalment out of, what, ten planned books? That’s only halfway through (behold my mathematic <i>genius</i>) and already so much has happened! And that’s only all we know of; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5265998.Shannon_Messenger" title="Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Shannon Messenger</a> stated she’d put out Keeper books for as long as she could. Part of me is worried that the quality might deteriorate if the series goes on too long but another part of me <b>never wants this to end</b>!<br /><br /><br /><b>P L O T</b><br /><br />Okay, so I had a little more trouble getting into this one than the last three. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27272698.Lodestar__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___5_" title="Lodestar (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #5) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Lodestar</a>’s plot lacked a definitive structure in which the characters had a plan worked out to achieve this one <b>major</b> objective. In this case, the characters didn’t have a plan—and of course they didn’t after what happened in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22733616.Neverseen__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___4_" title="Neverseen (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #4) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Neverseen</a> because <b>how does one construct a masterful scheme after such first-class mind-fuckery</b>?<br /><br />In that respect, it was totally realistic. It was a string of events that kind of just occurred suddenly for no particular reason. It was sporadic which conveyed the characters’ impulsive and frenzied actions. On the downside, it <i>did</i> make the story less memorable. In fact, the only reason I’m not giving this book 5 stars is for that reason; I honestly can’t remember maybe a third of what took place after just having read it.<br /><br />Regardless, it integrated so many sociopolitical views, exploring various prejudices and adding a whole new level of complexity by addressing the flaws of an otherwise seemingly idealistic world. Remember how I had a moan about the elves’ superiority complex back in my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12842828.Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___1_" title="Keeper of the Lost Cities (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #1) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Keeper of the Lost Cities</a> review? Yeah, can’t do that here.<br /><br />Also: how the SEVEN HELLS is Shannon Messenger so consistent with her excruciating cliffhangers? Every single book ends with <b>such</b> a bang that, from the moment I close the book, I’m antsy for the next one. Eventually, I am going to catch up with everyone else and have to... <i>ugh</i> <b>shudders</b> <i>Wait for the next book to be released</i>.<br /><br /><br /><b>C H A R A C T E R S</b><br /><br />Sophie Foster would be the ultimate Disney princess. I’m dead serious. She is such a sweetheart. She’s so kind to everyone, always tries to see the best in people, believes what she alone chooses to believe in no matter what anyone else thinks. Throughout, I was urging other characters to give her a hug (seeing as I, personally, am not a hugger) and felt so satisfied when Keefe, especially, delivered on that front. <b>I seriously adore her.</b> And them. Both of them.<br /><br />Ah, but here is the catch. The List of Things Sophie Gets That No One Else Does Because She’s Special is piling up againnnn:<br />Sophie sets the record for fastest splotcher burst, Sophie is the only one to trigger earthquakes, Sophie “has a unique role in many of the Elvin world’s most recent challenges”, Sophie’s presence was specifically requested at this summit thingie where only the one leader from each nation may attend, Sophie gets a private audience with Queen Hylda, Sophie gets another special ability (for real this time; not like the last few times where I joked about her having 4475892918274592 powers). <br /><br />But I almost don’t even care. <br /><br /><br /><i>Almost.</i><br /><br />Keefe. I missed Keefe. I love Keefe. I don’t know what else to say. <b>Keefe’s just the best, guys.</b> Did I mention that other peoples’ ravings about him is what gave me the final push to dedicate to this series? Because it was. And it totally delivered.<br /><br />Sadly enough, Fitz is even more boring than before. How is that possible? What is there to him, <i>really</i>? He’s a gorgeous talent with a temper. In a vague sense, I like him, but it’s been five books and by now I really should be able to say more than that about him.<br /><br />Biana is... pretty adorable. She’s girly but not strictly prissy, as shown by her handy dandy tackle tactic. She’s actually kind of a little devil girl and she’s finally sparked my interest. <br /><br /><b>Tam is described as being very similar to Keefe so I automatically really like him.</b> In my status update, I claimed I was joking about this but, the sad truth is, <b>I was 100% for real</b>. I have no shame. But, for real, I like Tam for reasons other than this as well. I really enjoy his general demeanour; there’s something about his presence alone that draws my complete and utter attention. His general look, his moodiness, how he hates the world but loves his sister to pieces and can’t fathom the idea of girls flirting with him. He makes for good comedy with his sarcasm, negativity and his <i>adorable</i> awkwardness.<br /><br />I wish I could say I liked said sister as much. Linh is noticeably more brief than Tam and I want to see so much more of her! From what I’ve got so far, I feel like I would really like her. She’s on the breathtaking cover of the next book, though, so here’s to hoping!<br /><br />I feel like majority of the adults are starting to become interchangeable which is kind of sad. They can be divided into three groups: <br />1. Those that support Sophie,<br />2. Those that don’t<br />3. And Grady.<br /><br />I was annoyed at Grady for being so hard on Keefe until I realised that it's because he sees the spark between Keefe and Sophie and he <i>hates</i> it. Not even with Fitz does he get so worked up because, case and point, Grady knows what’s up. He doesn’t bother to go all overprotective dad on Fitz’s ass—only on Keefe’s.<br /><br /><i>Look at me, getting ahead of myself with the shipping.</i><br /><br /><br /><b>R E L A T I O N S H I P S</b><br /><br /><i>“She threw her arms around his shoulders, hugging him as tight as she could. Maybe if she never let go, she could hold the broken pieces together.”</i><br /><br />Tam knows wassup, Mr. Forkle knows wassup, Grady knows wassup, Sandor knows wassup. And they’re only the ones that I have physical evidence of.<br /><br />1. Tam: on more than one occasion teases and or matter-of-factly addresses their obvious unique connection.<br /><i>“Sophie rubbed the knot under her ribs. “I know you don’t trust Keefe—“<br />“And I know you do,” Tam interrupted. “I get that you two are really, really close—“<br />“They’re not that close,” Fitz mumbled.<br />“Uh... sure...,” Tam said.”</i><br /><br />2. Mr. Forkle: basically leaves Sophie’s heart in Keefe’s hands.<br /><i>“Haven’t you realised that yet? That’s why you and Mr. Sencen work so well together. You both push each other to believe in yourselves.”</i><br /><br />3. Grady: directs the brunt of his animosity towards Keefe because he thinks he’s the dude who has a serious chance of getting together with his daughter.<br /><i>Any sentence with the phrase “That Boy” in it.</i><br /><br />4. Sandor: being serious but a sly thing with his probing Sophie to come clean. <br /><i>“Sophie giggled. “Man, I wish Keefe had been here to hear you say that.”<br />“Interesting that he was the first boy you thought of.”</i><br /><br />4.5. Grady <b>AND</b> Sandor: conspiratorially glancing at one another about how oblivious lil’ Sophie is.<br /><i>“In case you haven’t noticed, he teases everyone. It doesn’t mean anything. Especially with me.”<br />“You really believe that, don’t you?” Grady asked, glancing at Sandor when she nodded.<br />“If you guys look at each other like that again I’m going to punch you,” Sophie warned.”</i><br /><br />What can I say about Sokeefe that I haven’t said already? Not mu—actually, SO MUCH. But it requires discussing specifics which I obviously can’t do in a non-spoiler review, so... I think I’ll just leave it at their time apart in this book, while painful for my heart, has made their bond so much stronger. And also that I haven’t shipped anything this hard since friggin’ <b>Percabeth</b>.<br /><br />Also, THIS: <i>“I’m always serious, Foster. Especially when you think I’m teasing.”</i> <br />Honestly, how oblivious can one be?<br /><br /><i>“So.<br />Much.<br />Rage.<br />She wanted to bathe in it, drown in it, let the anger take control until she’d punished anyone and everyone who’d ever hurt her. But she’d held on to one thread of good through the barrage—one wisp of a thought that tethered her to who she needed to be.<br />Keefe.”</i><br /><br />I didn’t know whether to ship Biana with Tam or Dex at first. They’re both cute. Honestly, I don’t <i>HAVE</i> to ship her with anyone... but since when has that ever stopped me? <br /><br />See, the premise of Dex hating the Vackers but then falling in love with one, in theory, is very interesting indeed, but I’ve decided Tam and Biana are both devil children in their own ways and make a better team.<br /><br />I love how Fitz was wondering why Keefe reached out to Sophie and not to him. <i>(That was me being sarcastic.)</i> I mean, on one hand, I’m glad he’s showing a little remorse and care towards his relationship with his alleged best friend, but, on the other hand... <i>Really?</i> He repeatedly alienates Keefe (which I suppose I understand after the trust issues that would inevitably develop what with the Vacker family’s most recent devastation) and then when he assures him that he understands his actions, it all falls so flat. All of their interactions in Lodestar do, unfortunately.<br /><br />But <i>fortunately</i>, the Fitz-Biana friendship is <b>vastly</b> improving. For example, when she teases him mercilessly about his matchmaker process. That’s the kind of sibling banter I’m looking for!<br /><br />The Grady-Edaline-Sophie relationship warmed my heart yet again, Fitz quite literally 'wow'ing over Linh is not only hilarious but also ridiculously cute, and...<br /><br />As an afterthought, Fitz and Sophie are <b>meh</b> as ever. Her crush is still technically cute, but...<br /><br /><i>To whomever divine entity it may concern (I suppose that’s Shannon), <br /><br /><b>Do NOT</b> let Fitzphie be endgame.</i><br /><br />... ...<br /><br />The binge continues.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6097977634878930458" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1460150484?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lila" href="/user/show/34669718-lila">Lila</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

  <span id="freeText3742405812310765559" style="display:none">5 stars<br /><br />I promise someday to read a book that is not from this series. (Today is not that day.) Apologies to all of my Goodreads friends for just endlessly blasting these stories in your feed. I can’t stop reading them. This one was also great. <br /><br /><i>Lodestar</i> is the fifth book in Sophie Foster's adventures in the Keeper of the Lost Cities series, and in my opinion it just keeps upping the ante. <b>At this point, I'm honestly in awe of Shannon Messenger's relentless imagination. What can possibly happen next?</b> When will I get my questions answered about Sophie's role in her world? And MOST IMPORTANTLY, when will we finally get our Keefe/Sophie love arc? (There's another love interest named Fitz and let's just say he's not my favorite angle of the triangle.)<br /><br />I can't go into much about the details into <i>Lodestar</i> without running into at least one spoiler for the previous books, so just take my word for it when I say that Sophie's adventures in this one are great. Keefe's arc in this story is extremely angsty (so great) and the negative forces at play are incredibly devious (also great) and honestly not very middle grade in content—I think we're at the point in the series where if these books weren't connected to early books in the series aimed at younger readers, they'd be shelved as YA. Also, I definitely cried at the end due to a specific character death that I was NOT ready for—poor Sophie.<br /><br />If you're new to Keeper of the Lost Cities, check out my thoughts on the earlier books!<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2846444914" rel="nofollow noopener">Keeper of the Lost Cities (#1)</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2882274436" rel="nofollow noopener">Exile (#2)</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2882274758" rel="nofollow noopener">Everblaze (#3)</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2899169250" rel="nofollow noopener">Neverseen (#4)</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3742699957140156443"><b>5 Stars!</b><br/><br/>This SERIES! My god, I can't even begin to explain how unexpected this is. Honestly it's such a whirlwind of emotions, and by far, this book made me the most emotional!<br/><br/>Some points;<br/>- Keefe and Sandor remain strong favourites. <br/>- Sophie is becoming such a stronger character in the sense that I'm beginning to like her a lot more<br/>- We see more of Tam in this book and THAT is something that liked, his ability is SO interesting and I need more please<br/>- All of the unraveling, I've said before I fo</span>
  <span id="freeText3742699957140156443" style="display:none"><b>5 Stars!</b><br /><br />This SERIES! My god, I can't even begin to explain how unexpected this is. Honestly it's such a whirlwind of emotions, and by far, this book made me the most emotional!<br /><br />Some points;<br />- Keefe and Sandor remain strong favourites. <br />- Sophie is becoming such a stronger character in the sense that I'm beginning to like her a lot more<br />- We see more of Tam in this book and THAT is something that liked, his ability is SO interesting and I need more please<br />- All of the unraveling, I've said before I found some of the books and plot points a bit predictable, this however had my jaw to the floor and being like oh my god, and cursing quite a lot!<br />- I don't know what it is with this series BUT the last 100 pages are always INCREDIBLE, I can't explain, I know books are supposed to draw you in, but the endings always have me gagged and I <b>love</b> it.<br />- How to word this, I don't know so the easiest way is to say we see more; Goblins, Ogres, Dwarves, Neverseen, Gnomes it was just brilliant!<br />- Silver Pants and dancing, this I need to see<br />- Even though there's serious moments we still have some light hearted parts which is very nice!<br /><br />Overall, I can hands down say I am loving this series, it's just so gripping and once you're in your hooked! I'm taking a very short break to read Radio Silence with Alexis (which I am very very excited about), but I can't wait to pick up the next book!</span>

HE IS A CUTE CINNAMON ROLL CHILD! I LOVE HIM! HE JUST MAKES EVERYTHING BETTER<br /><br />10. TAM! Since I actually kinda RP as Keefe, I have sorta had a feud with him. <div id="review_1719354964" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1719354964" />
    <a title="malayna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55992181-malayna"><img alt="malayna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592140082p2/55992181.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1719354964?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="malayna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="malayna" href="/user/show/55992181-malayna">malayna</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55992181-malayna?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1719354964" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11330474586705343949">UPDATED REVIEW<br/><br/>MY OPINION: *****<br/><br/>This is my second time reading this book (the newest one just came out and I'm trying to reread the series to mentally prepare myself). <br/><br/>I've been reading this series since I was in fifth grade (I'm not in high school). Although this series is a mix of Middle Grade and Young Adult, it holds a lot of sentimentality and emotional memories. I mean, this used to be my life. I wrote fanfiction on this series, I was (and still am) a diehard Sophitz shipper, and I was in e</span>
  <span id="freeText11330474586705343949" style="display:none">UPDATED REVIEW<br /><br />MY OPINION: *****<br /><br />This is my second time reading this book (the newest one just came out and I'm trying to reread the series to mentally prepare myself). <br /><br />I've been reading this series since I was in fifth grade (I'm not in high school). Although this series is a mix of Middle Grade and Young Adult, it holds a lot of sentimentality and emotional memories. I mean, this used to be my life. I wrote fanfiction on this series, I was (and still am) a diehard Sophitz shipper, and I was in every KOTLC fandom ever. <br /><br />Now, as an older person, I can appreciate the parts of the book that I never used to care about (i.e. the government system in this book) and draw connections to how Messenger created a world that was so different and yet so similar to our world as we know it now.<br /><br />Can I just talk about the memories that rereading this book brought back?<br /><br />Fitz was still as dreamy as ever. Biana was still as excitable and gorgeous as I remember her. I still held my normal love-hate relationship with Dex. I already had forgiven Keefe and was excited to see where he would go. Tam was my favorite twin and Linh was just as sweet as I remembered. I'm so excited to start the sixth and seventh books because those are the two that I never ended up getting around to after all this time.<br /><br />I mean, KOTLC was the birth of my Goodreads. I started on GR confused and I found so many other KOTLC fandom accounts that I got my start here and for that I am so thankful. Without it, I would never have met so many awesome readers and gotten to love/hate so many amazing/not-so-amazing books.<br /><br />This book really dealt with a lot. It really got into how the government system was completely falling apart (similar to many governments today) and how the leaders of an entire world were struggling to keep up their appearances and good reputations. It shows how the world was corrupt and how the people really had no say in anything that the Councillors did. I loved how it was an accurate representation of the trials and tribulations that comes with being either a leader of a country/nation/society or a citizen. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[NOOOOO POOR MR FORKLE <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Sophitz Forever (I mean, if you want to find my old stuff, you can still find my Sophitz Forever story on my FanFiction.net account ---@malaynamonkey2004--- or my Wattpad account (which has the updated version)---@malaynaturally---so go ahead and find that)<br /><br />Aww and Sandor and Grizel are so cute<br /><br />I'm so excited to read the next books and I would recommend this series to people looking for a lighthearted/dramatic fantasy series.<br /><br />Main Character: Sophie<br />Sidekick(s): Fitz, Dex, Biana, Tam, Linh, Keefe, Grady, Mr. Forkle, etc<br />Villain(s): Corrupt government, Fintan, Brant, Ruy, Alvar, Neverseen, etc<br />Fantasy Elements: This book was based on fanatic elements.<br /><br />********************************************************************************<br /><br />MY OPINION: *****<br /><br />OK, I have to say something that I say repeatedly: THIS BOOK WAS AMAZING!<br /><br />OK, I want to start with the spoilers first, but before I start, I want to say to all of you one thing. I am aiming this post towards the people who have finished the book already. It will be filled with spoilers. I will mark them, but that won't leave a lot for you to read if you haven't finished the book (unless you want to read the spoilers). Also, this post is also aimed towards people who have read and commented on Goodreads on this book. Lastly, if you have no plans to read this book, I would read the post! By all means, go for it!<br /><br />SPOILER ALERT!!!<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Sophitz is as good as sailed!<br /><br />I don't know if this is actually a spoiler because, I guess, it is kind of obvious that Sophie would end up with most of them. But I will still cross it out anyways.<br /><br />Sophitz was EVERYWHERE in this book! OK, first of all, I am totally going to start at her near-kiss with Fitz:<br /><br />Page 666 (OH NO - IT'S THE BAD NUMBER! WHY??????)<br /><br />"We could skip the talking...He was so close now, she could feel his breath warming her cheeks...He leaned a tiny bit closer and someone cleared his throat—very loudly..."<br /><br />KEEFE!!!!!! WHY???? They were SO close!!!!! Keefe had to go and ruin everything. Again. Keefe, why do you have to do this to me?<br /><br />This book brings out too much emotion from me. I was literally screaming at the book while reading :)<br /><br />Also, this book is perfectly appropriate for kids, so no worries.<br /><br />Anyways, there are LOTS of other Sophitz moments, but I only enclosed the best, and saved the rest for you to FIND! PLEASE COMMENT IF YOU FIND ANY COOL SOPHITZ MOMENTS!<br /><br />By the way, Sophitz is Sophie+Fitz, in case you didn't know :)<br /><br />Now, on my way!<br /><br />MR. FORKLE DIES!!!<br /><br />NOOOOOOOOOOO!!!!!! My life has ended! Why??? Mr. Forkle, the kind and clever Mr. Forkle (AKA Sir Astin, AKA Magnate Leto, etc). Also, why Gethen? Why did he have to be the one to do it? I just don't get it. The Black Swan, and Sophie, needs Mr. Forkle! He is like the heart of the group, and without the heart, the group DIES. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />How I wish I could spoil freely!<br /><br />Now I will talk with no spoilers.<br /><br />Tam and Linh become much bigger characters in this book. Tam even accompanies Sophie and Fitz on capturing two of the Neverseen. *SIGH*. Spoilers are literally everywhere.<br /><br />I feel like Sophitz's only competition is Fitz and Linh, and after reading this book, I feel like that will NEVER happen.<br /><br />Fitz is old enough to get his Matchmaker's Scroll! But as much as I want that to happen, I'm glad he is going to wait at least 2 years. *COUGH* (SOPHIE HAS 2 MORE YEARS TO GO)! YAY!<br /><br />Ok, enough Sophitz. Sorry for anyone who doesn't ship Sophie with Fitz. :(<br /><br />More Spoilers...<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Sophie becomes an Enhancer! Personally, I don't like the idea of her new ability. I mean, it doesn't really help her at all, unless she is with others, and even then, what if it is the bad guys? Also, I don't really like the idea of her adding a new ability.<br /><br />Every time Sophie gets a new ability, I feel like that is going to change her in some way, and she will never be the same person again. I know that Shannon Messenger has a way to work it all out, but I'm always so afraid that her new ability will confuse the whole story. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Fitz is a HUGE character in this story. I just love all the Cognate training he does with Sophie! (*ARGHHH* NO MORE SOPHITZ). Sorry, can't help it :)<br /><br />I also like how Shannon gives Dex an important role in the story. I don't really like Dex as much as Fitz or Keefe, but I am glad that Dex had a bigger character, because I always feel like Dex is left out a lot. I mean, other than the first book, he doesn't really accompany Sophie alone on any important missions, while basically all of the other team members have.<br /><br />I can't say anything about Keefe (SPOILERS), but I will state that Keefe is still an amazing guy, despite his mistakes.<br /><br />OOH, a little romance occurs with Sandor and Grizel. Sorry if you consider that a spoiler :)<br /><br />So it does turn out that if you haven't read the book, you still have stuff to read. READ ON<br /><br />This book had an amazing plot line. I started this series last year, maybe, and I still think it is amazing. The only problem is, as my reading matures, I feel like the context is a bit under my level. Then again, even though it doesn't help me grow my reading level, I can still enjoy a wonderful book, AND it takes less time to read!!!! So I guess it is a Win-Win situation.<br /><br />I have to talk about the problems with the other species. I mean, although Shannon says that the elves hate violence, but it isn't really a book without any action. Shannon does do a great job of describing how the elves have many disagreements, and it sort of reminds me of the real world. Violence is going to be everywhere, and no matter how hard we avoid it, someone is going to start something. But what we can do is try out best to stop it by doing something helpful out of kindness instead of anger. PEACE. LOVE.<br /><br />Anyways, with everything that has happened so far, it leaves me no choice except to say that I sort of dislike some of the Council members right now. I know they mean well, but sometimes, you just can't force yourself to like someone, especially if they have made many mistakes that wouldn't have happened if they had paused to listen to their own PEOPLE (or I guess, ELVES!). I really hope that the Council redeems themselves by the next 2 books.<br /><br />BTW, SHANNON MESSENGER JUST RELEASED THAT SHE IS GOING TO RELEASE A SIXTH AND SEVENTH BOOK OF THE SERIES!!!!!! YES!!!!! I cannot wait. The sad thing is, I have to wait another year for the 6th book and 2 years for the 7th book.<br /><br />I really enjoyed reading this book. It was truly an amazing experience. The one thing that I really enjoyed about this whole series is:<br /><br />THIS SERIES IS SO UNPREDICTABLE.<br /><br />When I read, I find that the book is always really easy to know what is going to happen, but in the KOTLC series, there are so many possibilities that plot twisters still make me fall out of my chair!<br /><br />I would recommend this book to anyone who loves a little talent, humor, romance, and action mixed into one incredible adventure. It is definitely a book that will interest you, no matter how young or old, even though the series is geared for middle-schoolers.<br /><br />Main Character: Sophie Foster<br />Sidekick(s): Fitz Vacker, Dex Dizznee, Keefe Sencen, Tam Song, Linh Song, Mr. Forkle, Edaline, Grady, Alden, Della, Sandor, Grizel, etc<br />Villain(s): Neverseen (Fintan, Brant, Alvar, Ruy, Gethen, Trix, etc)<br />Fantasy Elements: Unreal creatures, unreal settings, unreal elements.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11330474586705343949" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2583808776" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2583808776" />
    <a title="Maddie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60336580-maddie"><img alt="Maddie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498658110p2/60336580.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2583808776?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maddie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maddie" href="/user/show/60336580-maddie">Maddie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2583808776" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2517317607820586753">3.5<br/><br/>I said in my review of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2158185805' rel='nofollow noopener'>Book 4</a> that every book in this series is both a major step forwards and a major step backwards. Book 5 is a major step forwards and a normal sized step backwards. <br/><br/>- I think this series has an issue with intentionality. A lot of the things I would identify as this series’s strengths are things I don’t believe were done intentionally. The fact that a lot of the things discussed in earlier books/themes from earlier books/etc don’t carry over into later books really solidif</span>
  <span id="freeText2517317607820586753" style="display:none">3.5<br /><br />I said in my review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2158185805" rel="nofollow noopener">Book 4</a> that every book in this series is both a major step forwards and a major step backwards. Book 5 is a major step forwards and a normal sized step backwards. <br /><br />- I think this series has an issue with intentionality. A lot of the things I would identify as this series’s strengths are things I don’t believe were done intentionally. The fact that a lot of the things discussed in earlier books/themes from earlier books/etc don’t carry over into later books really solidified this for me.<br />- Relatedly, I think a lot of the red herrings in this series are more interesting than what actually winds up being the truth.<br />- I’ve also noticed a big tonality shift as the books progress. Books 4 and 5 both feature a lot of dialogue/language and scenarios/tropes that are extremely endemic of “fanfiction written by a 13 year old”. This is totally fine in theory, but if you're trying to write an epic fantasy, its distracting and seems out of place.<br />- I think there is a problem when Tam and Linh (who we first met in Book 4) and Wylie (who had three very small appearances in previous books) are better developed characters than Dex, Fitz and Biana, who have been prominent characters since Book 1. I thought all three got <i>some</i> development in Books 4 and 5 (especially Biana, who really shined in Book 5 despite her minimal page-time), but it's still not quite enough to justify them being such important characters. I thought the reveal at the end of Book 4 would force all of the Vackers to undergo some major character development, but it didn’t. <br />- A lot of what made the first few books compelling (Foxfire and the adult characters) have become smaller elements of the series, which I think is a problem. It's fine to change your mind or want to explore other settings and characters, but you shouldn't abandon a setting that was pitched as the focal point of the series or sideline almost all of the adult characters/completely change the characterization of the adult characters (Grady...) for no good reason. There's a difference between changing your mind/exploring new ideas and completely abandoning any semblance of consistency. <br />- I've noticed many of the books in this series have identical issues with pacing. I think it's especially noticeable in Books 3-5, which both get off to extremely slow starts. Similarly, there are lot of things that happen in these books that should probably be given more page-time to be digested/discussed/etc that are immediately glossed over (like I don't know, Keefe getting branded? Everything involving Wylie?) These books are large and theoretically have enough page-time to devote to these things, but don't. Not giving these things more focus creates this weird kind of emotional whiplash, and I always finish each book feeling a bit unsettled. <br />- I’ve always maintained that Fitz was an “I’m only interested when I know someone else is interested, especially if that someone else is my (best) friend” love interest. I’ve never seen that trope play out as blatantly and transparently as it did in this book. <br />- The love triangle/square is also getting progressively grating as the books go on and the characters get older. I think part of my difficultly with it is that I’m struggling to figure out just what Messenger is trying to do with it. Considering that this series already has issues with contradictory themes and characterizations, I think the way the love triangle is being presented only makes these issues worse.<br /><br />Overall, I think this one of the more solid book in the series. It may not be the most enjoyable (I think that was Book 2), but a lot of the problems in the previous books, while still present in this book, were significantly less noticeable/distracting. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2517317607820586753" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1818793025" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1818793025" />
    <a title="Kristen Kooistra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51941369-kristen-kooistra"><img alt="Kristen Kooistra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487706914p2/51941369.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1818793025?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristen Kooistra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen Kooistra" href="/user/show/51941369-kristen-kooistra">Kristen Kooistra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1818793025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1733737990716664260">I unashamedly LOVE KotLC. All of my friends are probably sick of hearing me say it by now. Reading this series is like coming home on a cold winter night and climbing into your nice toasty bed under piles of blankets. It's what I look forward too, it's familiar, it never disappoints. <br/><br/>Full review on <a href='http://kristenkooistra.blogspot.com/2016/12/lodestarkeeper-of-lost-cities-5-abb.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>my blog.</a><br/><br/>I bought Lodestar because I couldn't stand waiting in the massive line to check it out at the library(it took me forever to get Neverseen) and because at this stage, it'd take a miracle for Sh</span>
  <span id="freeText1733737990716664260" style="display:none">I unashamedly LOVE KotLC. All of my friends are probably sick of hearing me say it by now. Reading this series is like coming home on a cold winter night and climbing into your nice toasty bed under piles of blankets. It's what I look forward too, it's familiar, it never disappoints. <br /><br />Full review on <a href="http://kristenkooistra.blogspot.com/2016/12/lodestarkeeper-of-lost-cities-5-abb.html" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog.</a><br /><br />I bought Lodestar because I couldn't stand waiting in the massive line to check it out at the library(it took me forever to get Neverseen) and because at this stage, it'd take a miracle for Shannon Messenger to majorly fail me. <br /><br />Lodestar was even better than Neverseen. There was lots of little pieces that really hit home for me. I love Shannon's ability to not only create a completely engaging story that draws in even old people like me, but also that she finds a way to add elements that we all so desperately need to see in fiction. She makes them easy to understand and does it naturally so that it's not like she's hitting me over the head with a moral.<br /><br />For example, one of Dex's brothers is being flirty and goes to wrap his arm around Biana. It's a little thing and completely appropriate for a MG audience. And Dex's dad steps in and says, "No, we do not touch women without their permission." It fit the story, it was easy to slip in there, and it's a good way to show a young audience(or an older one) that it's not okay to just touch people in a "sensual" way without asking. It showed a perfect example so people won't be confused with friends hugging, or high fives, etc.<br /><br />I loved getting to see more of Dex's family and some of the non-elvin cultures. I was really hoping that Sophie would take Lady Cadence's advice to heart and was sad that things had to end the way they did with a particular group(trying to avoid spoilers).<br /><br />Mysteries are solved, and new mysteries are born. Shannon did a great job of giving me some answers while creating enough questions where again I'm sitting here wishing that the next book was out already. <br /><br />I miss Dex. He's been sidelined the past two books and I'm sure that's just to start narrowing down who Sophie ends up with and shift more people to Keefe or Fitz. I'm not a fan, at all, of love triangles(I even went so far last book to call it a square and laughed when a character called it that in Lodestar). Luckily, Shannon puts very little emphasis on it and Sophie's not leading anyone along. It's been obvious from the very start that Fitz has always been the one she's got a crush on. And crush is what it is. Sophie was like what . . . 11? 12? in the first book. She's a child and I'm not in a hurry to matchmake for a child and I'm quite happy to see her just be Sophie(though Dophie made me laugh also) for now.<br /><br />Maybe in 4-5 years or so she'll be ready for a real romantic relationship and realize she's been blind to the awesomeness that is Dex.<br /><br />And kudos to Shannon for adding in the scene where Sophie stands up to the Songs. I read that part to my mom and my husband because what Sophie says can be applied to so many situations and it really struck home. It's a message that kids need when parents have failed to be parents. They need to know they're worth more. They need to know that they can stand on their own and there's nothing wrong with separating themselves from harmful parents(if possible). Adults need to know this too! <br /><br />I'm so excited to see 2 more books are at least going to be added!! I hope this series never ends. I'd be happy to read about an 18 year old Sophie, and a 20 year old sophie, and considering Elves live forever, let's be real, who wouldn't be happy to read about Sophie for the rest of our lives at any age?<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1733737990716664260" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1733722527" class="readable"

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7808972207285655576">1.) Keeper of the Lost Cities ★★★★★<br/>2.) Exile ★★★★★<br/>3.) Everblaze ★★★★★<br/>4.) Neverseen ★★★★<br/><br/>Reveiw Update: October 2018<br/>After the fourth time reading this, I’ve decided that its a fact that the KEEPER books keep getting better with every book.<br/><br/>Original Reveiw - November 1st 2016<br/>Dear Shannon Messenger,<br/><br/>Since the first moment I got this book I started reading it, so I've been reading it for about 13 hours. its around five in the morning where I live and well I don't think I'm going to fall asleep. Around </span>
  <span id="freeText7808972207285655576" style="display:none">1.) Keeper of the Lost Cities ★★★★★<br />2.) Exile ★★★★★<br />3.) Everblaze ★★★★★<br />4.) Neverseen ★★★★<br /><br />Reveiw Update: October 2018<br />After the fourth time reading this, I’ve decided that its a fact that the KEEPER books keep getting better with every book.<br /><br />Original Reveiw - November 1st 2016<br />Dear Shannon Messenger,<br /><br />Since the first moment I got this book I started reading it, so I've been reading it for about 13 hours. its around five in the morning where I live and well I don't think I'm going to fall asleep. Around 75-78 chapter I was so tired and I thought I should pick it up when I got some sleep. But I didn't but do you know what happen.<br /><br />MR.FORCLE (sorry if I butchered his name) DIED<br />HE'S DEAD<br /><br />BUT KEEFE IS GOOD AND BACK AND NOW FITZ CAN'T GO SHAMELESSY FLIRTING WITH SOPHIE WITHOUT HER KNOWING AND YOU WOULD THINK ALL WAS RIGHT WITH THE WORLD, RIGHT?<br /><br />NO BECAUSE THEY (The Neverseen) HAVE HER HUMAN PARENTS AND NOW HER SISTER IS BACK IN THE EQUATION AND WHAT IS GOING TO HAPPEN!<br /><br />One day, when I'm an author, I'm going to write your favorite book series of all time and you know what I'm going to do? I GOING TO PUT YOU IN THE SITUATION YOU NOW PUT ME AND ALL YOUR OTHER READERS IN AND I'M GOING TO HAVE A MESSAGE FOR YOU AND YOU'LL HAVE TO WAIT AND FIND OUT!<br /><br />Also PLEASE PLEASE PLEASE um teleport all of us Keepers to the future so we can read your books? Please and Thank<br />You!<br /><br />Forever a Keeper,<br />Sage <br /><br />P.S HOW COME SOPHIE DIDN'T KISS ANYONE IN THIS BOOK BECAUSE ITS ABOUT TIME ONE OF THE TWO DUDE THAT EVERYONE IN THE FANDOM IS ARGUING ABOUT FINALLY GET TO KISS HER !(hopeful Keefe)</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gan51RHD6ubCn3NKL2iWdWB7twGAr+VxlT+ueTjpafwr1HREv4sdZiWgEHUoLWiDeccPyDSP+K05LKSIKTQ3tg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VrAlWDiuMI9hmSnKQulvkDDtd03frvudKtcagEG9Rcz8zajJlubHD4amSvVFrJFmKVHPhGuO5kGGxBBxUGAbhg==')})
  }
//]]>
